Eggeling
  1. Tvashс╣нr╠е, seeing his son slain, brought Soma suitable for witchery, and withheld from Indra. Indra, committing a desecration of the sacrifice, by main force drank off his (Tvashс╣нr╠е’s) Soma juice. He went asunder in every direction,–from his mouth and vital airs his excellence and fame passed

away, and entered the cattle, whence cattle are one’s fame: and famous, indeed, is he who, knowing this, is consecrated 8 by the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л.

Eggeling
  1. It is made of udumbara wood, for the udumbara (ficus glomerata) is strength: for the sake of strength he thus is consecrated. It is knee-high, for knee-high is this (terrestrial) world, and it is for (the rule of) this world that the Kshatriya is consecrated; and the ruler (kshatra) indeed he becomes who is consecrated by the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л: therefore it is knee-high, and of unlimited size horizontally (in width and depth),–

Eggeling
  1. For the throne-seat means royal dignity, and of unlimited prosperity is royal dignity. It is covered with plaited reed-work, for reed-grass is meet for sacrifice. Two of its feet stand on the

northern, and two on the southern altar-ground 10, for the northern vedi is this (terrestrial) world, and the southern one the world of the Fathers: he thus consecrates him for both worlds.

Eggeling
  1. There are hoof-cups (of gravy), for on hoofs cattle support themselves: he thus causes him to obtain a support. There are thirty-three (such)

cupfuls, for thirty-three in number are all the deities: by means of all the deities he thus consecrates him. He offers them with jagat─л verses, for animals are of j─Бgata (movable) nature: by means of the Jagat─л he thus secures cattle for him. With sixteen verses (V─Бj. S. XIX, 80-94) he offers, for animals are of sixteen parts: he thus bestows excellence (or prosperity) on him part by part.

Eggeling
  1. He sprinkles him (with the fat gravy) in front while (himself) looking towards the back (west), for

from the front food is visibly eaten. On. every side (he sprinkles him) whilst moving round: he thus bestows food on him from all quarters, whence food is secured from all quarters by him who has performed the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л, or even by him who thus knows this.

Eggeling
  1. With a formula to the A┼Ыvins he sprinkles him first 18, then with one to Sarasvat─л, then with one to Indra: it is by means of these deities he thus consecrates him. Now, some consecrate him by means both of these deities and those utterances, ‘bh┼лс╕е bhuvaс╕е, svar,’ ‘for,’ say they, ’these utterances (“earth, air, heaven”) mean all this (universe) it is by means of all this (universe) we thus consecrate him.’ Let him, however, not do so, but let him only consecrate him by means of those deities, for those deities, indeed, are all this (universe).

Eggeling
  1. He consecrates him prior to the Svishс╣нakr╠еt (offering), for the Svishс╣нakr╠еt is the Kshatra: he thus consecrates him by means of the Kshatra (or, by a Kshatriya). And he consecrates him between (the oblation to) the Lord of the Forest 19 and the

Svishс╣нakr╠еt, for the lord of the forest (or the tree) is Soma, and the Svishс╣нakr╠еt (maker of good offering) is Agni: he thus consecrates him after encompassing him by Agni and Soma; whence both those who know, and those who do not, say, ‘A Kshatriya is the consecrator of a Kshatriya 20.’

  1. As to this they say, ‘But, surely, he who is consecrated by the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л moves away from this world.’ Well, he descends again upon the black antelope skin, and, the black antelope skin being the sacrifice, he thus finally establishes himself on the sacrifice.

рд╣рд░рд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА

[рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдирдВ рдирд╡рджрд╢реЗ]

Eggeling
  1. [He descends 23, with V─Бj. S. XX, 10,] ‘Firmly 24 I establish myself in the Kshatra (lordship), in royal sway,’–in lordship and royal sway he thus establishes himself so as not to lose lordship and royal sway;–‘firmly in horses I establish

myself, and in kine,’–in the midst of horses and kine he thus establishes himself so as not to lose horses and kine;–‘firmly in the limbs I establish myself, and in the body,’–in the limbs and in the body he thus establishes himself so as not to lose his limbs and his body;–‘firmly in the vital airs I establish myself, and in prosperity,’–in the vital airs and in prosperity he thus establishes himself so as not to lose the vital airs and prosperity;–‘firmly in heaven and on earth I establish myself, and in the sacrifice,’–he thus establishes himself in these two, heaven and earth, within which is all this (universe).

Eggeling
  1. He 25 then sings a S─Бman (hymn-tune), for the S─Бman means lordship (kshatra): with lordship he thus consecrates him; or the S─Бman means imperial sway: by means of imperial sway he thus causes him to attain imperial sway. And, indeed, the S─Бman is the essence of all the Vedas: he thus consecrates him with the essence of all the Vedas.

Eggeling
  1. him in these worlds. There are four fiс╣Зale┼Ы, for there are four quarters: they thus establish him in all the quarters. All (the priests) join in the fiс╣Зale: with one mind they thus bestow excellence upon him.

Eggeling
  1. Or he (the Adhvaryu) takes a thirty-third cupful (of gravy), with (V─Бj. S. XX, 11-12 32), ‘Thrice

eleven are the gods,’–for there are indeed thrice eleven gods;–’three-and-thirty, bountiful,’–for there are thirty-three gods; ‘with Br╠еhaspati for their Purohita,’–Br╠еhaspati is the Brahman (n.): he thus means to say, ‘With the Brahman for their Purohita (family-priest);’–‘at the impulse (sava) of the god Savitr╠е,’–that is, ‘impelled by the god Savitr╠е;’–‘may the gods protect me through the gods!’ for the gods indeed consecrate him through the gods.

рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпреИрд░рд┐рддрд┐ ред рдкрд░реЛ рд╜рд╡рд░рдВ рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рд░рдпрд╛ рдЖрджреНрдпрдпрд╛ рдкрд░рдпрд╛ рдЪреЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдВ рдкрд░реЛ рд╜рд╡рд░рдореН ред рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд┐рдЪреНрдп ред рдЕрдерд░реНрддреНрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрднреВрддреЗрд╖реБ рдЙрдкрд╣рд╡рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ “рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордиреНрдиреБрдкрд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╕реНрд╡” “рд╣реЛрддрд░реБрдкрд╣реНрд╡рдпрд╕реНрд╡” рдЗрддреНрдпреЗрд╡рдорд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердпрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рее рейреж рее

Eggeling
  1. ‘The first with the second,’–for the first (gods, on earth) consecrate him along with the second ones (in the air);–’the second with the third,’–for the second ones consecrate him along with the third ones (in the sky);–’the third with 33 the truth,’–for the third ones consecrate him with the truth;–’the truth with the sacrifice,’–for the truth consecrates him with the sacrifice;–’the sacrifice with sacrificial texts,’–for the sacrifice consecrates him with sacrificial texts;–‘sacrificial texts with hymn-tunes,’–for sacrificial texts (yajus) consecrate him along with hymn-tunes ‘hymn-tunes with hymn-verses,’–for hymn-tunes consecrate him along with hymn-verses (r╠еc):–‘hymn-verses with invitatory verses,’–for hymn-verses consecrate him along with invitatory verses;–‘invitatory verses with offering-verses,’–for invitatory verses consecrate him along with offering-verses;–‘offering-verses with Vashaс╣н-calls,’–for offering-verses consecrate him

along with Vashaс╣н-calls;–‘Vashaс╣н-calls with oblations,’–for Vashaс╣н-calls consecrate him along with oblations;–‘May the oblations render successful my wishes! bh┼лс╕е! sv─Бh─Б!’–having thus consecrated him by means of those deities from first to last, he thus, by means of oblations, renders all his wishes successful. Having then solicited an invitation from the officiating priests, he (the Sacrificer) drinks 34 (the remains of the cup of vas─Б), for the officiating priests are the seasons: it is thus in the seasons that he solicits art invitation.

рд╕ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐ ред “рд▓реЛрдорд╛рдирд┐ рдкреНрд░рдпрддрд┐рд░реНрдордо рддреНрд╡рдЩреНрдо рдЖрдирддрд┐рд░рд╛рдЧрддрд┐рдГ ред рдорд╛рдВрд╕рдВ рдо рдЙрдкрдирддрд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐ рдордЬреНрдЬрд╛ рдо рдЖрдирддрд┐рдГ”- ред (рд╡рд╛реж рд╕рдВреж реиреж ред резрей) рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реЗрд╡ рд╡рд╛ рдПрд╖ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд┐ ред рдпрдГ рд╕реМрддреНрд░рд╛рдордгреНрдпрд╛ рд╜рднрд┐рд╖рд┐рдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрджреЗрддрджрд╡рд╛рдВрддрд░рд╛рдорд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдореБрдкрд╣реНрд╡рдпрддреЗ ред рддрдерд╛ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрди рдПрд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддрдиреВрдГ рд╕рд╛рдВрдЧрдГ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддрд┐ рее рейрез рее

‘рд╕ рднрдХреНрд╖рдпрддрд┐’ ред рдпрдГ рд╕реМрддреНрд░рд╛рдордгреНрдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд┐рд╖рд┐рдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдиреН рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╢рддрд┐ ред (рддрд╛рд╕реНрд╡рдЙрдкрд╡реЗрд╢рд╛ ?) рдЗрддреНрдпрдЧреНрд░реЗ рдЙрдкрд╣реНрд╡рдпрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░рджрд╛рдирд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд╕реМрддреНрд░рд╛рдордгреНрдпрд╛ рдпрд╛рдЧреЗрдирд╛рджрдГ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдВрдЧрдВ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрдордиреНрдпреВрдирдВ рд╕рдВрднрд╡рддрд┐ рее рейрез рее

Eggeling
  1. He drinks it, with (V─Бj. S. XX, 13), ‘My hair is endeavour 35, my skin submission and approach 36, my flesh inclination, my bone wealth, and my marrow submission,’–for he who is consecrated by the Sautr─Бmaс╣З─л enters the worlds and among the deities; he now has himself, invited amongst them 37, and thus he arises (in the other world) complete, with a whole body, and with (all) limbs.

  29. 256:3 These words–apparently meaning ‘for fame all round, for fame far and wide, for true fame, for fame’ (or, perhaps, for hearing, or, rather, being heard of all round,’ &c.)–are used to form the fiс╣Зale┼Ы (nidhana) in which all the priests are to join; cf. S─Бmav., Calc. ed., I, pp. 533-4, where the figured text is given. According to Katy. XIX, 5, 4-5; L─Бс╣нy. V, 4, 19, the words, ‘saс╣Бjityai, vijityai, satyajityai, jityai’ (for complete victory, victory far and wide, &c.), and ‘sampushс╣нyai, vipushс╣нyai,’ &c. (for complete prosperity, &c.), are to be used instead, in the case of a Kshatriya and Vai┼Ыya respectively, either optionally or necessarily. Though these four words are here, and elsewhere, spoken of as so many different S─Бmans, only ’the last of them (‘┼Ыravase’) forms the fiс╣Зale of a S─Бman in the ordinary sense of the word; the others being merely combined with certain musical ejaculations, or expletives (stobhas). All the four ‘S─Бmans’ begin with the same phrase (varying only in the verb)–‘saс╣Б tv─Б hinvanti (riс╣Зanti, tatakshur, ┼Ыi┼Ыanti) dh─лtibhiс╕е,’ i, e. ’they make thee up (or urge thee on) with prayers,’ serving as a kind of prelude (prast─Бva) the single words of which are given among the Stobhas (S─БmavтАЮ Calc. ed., II, p. 522, last line), as, indeed, the words ‘saс╣Б┼Ыravase,’ &c., themselves are (ib., p. 520). In the first three S─Бmans this phrase is followed by the fiс╣Зale consisting of the respective characteristic word preceded by the Stobha ‘auhov─Б.’ In the last S─Бman, on the other hand, the introductory phrase is followed by the choral setting of the verse ‘Br╠еhad indr─Бya g─Бyata’ (see p. 255, n. 2), which, in its turn, is followed again by the first phrase, with a slightly modified modulation, ending with ‘auhov─Б ┼Ыravase.’ Whilst joining in the fiс╣Зale, the priests, according to L─Бс╣нy. V, 4, 17, are to lay their hands on the head of the Sacrificer. ↩︎
